The Fifth Proof for the Succession of Instants
Razi enumerates the fifth proof for the succession of instants via geometrical reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth proof for the succession of instants based on the motion of an epicycle center and its implications for atomic substance and time.

Core Idea
A point tracing a circle forces successive points and contiguous instants.

This lesson presents the fifth proof from Razi's al-Matalib al-Aliyah. Using a geometric argument from astronomy, Razi demonstrates that the continuous motion of a point implies a discrete structure of space and time. We will follow his reasoning step by step to see how it simultaneously establishes the indivisible substance (al-jawhar al-fard) and the succession of instants (tatali al-anat).

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own flow come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise argumentative style of Razi.
2
Understand the astronomical setup
Identify the key elements: the center of the epicycle is a point; when the carrier orb moves, this point traces a circle (the 'carrier circle' of the epicycle center).
The epicycle is a term from Ptolemaic astronomy; here it's used as a geometric object.
3
Follow the logical chain for space
The point touches all parts of the circle. Since only a point can touch a point, the circle must be composed of points. Therefore, a line (the circumference) is composed of contiguous points, which implies the indivisible substance (atomism in space).
This is a key step: from continuous motion to discrete composition.
4
Apply the same logic to time
The successive contacts between the center point and the points of the circle occur in successive instants. Since contact is instantaneous, those instants must be contiguous, proving the succession of instants (atomism in time).
This links space and time atomism.
5
Reflect on the proof's significance
Consider how this single proof elegantly ties together two fundamental doctrines of kalam: the indivisible substance and the discrete nature of time. Ask yourself: What assumptions does this proof rely on?
The proof assumes a point is indivisible and that contact between points is point-to-point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة في إثبات تتالي الآنات: أن نقول: لا شك أن مركز كرة التدوير نقطة. فإذا تحرك الفلك الحامل، فإنه يرتسم من حركة مركز التدوير دائرة، تسمى في علم الهيئة بالدائرة الحاملة لمركز التدوير، وتلك الدائرة بجميع أجزائها صارت ممسوسة لتلك النقطة. لكن النقطة لا يماسها إلا نقطة، فلما كانت هذه النقطة التي هي المركز، قد مست بجميع أجزاء تلك الدائرة، وثبت أن المماسة ما حصلت إلا على النقطة، وجب القطع بأن تلك الدائرة مرتسمة من النقط المتوالية، وذلك يقتضي كون الخط مركباً من النقط المتلاقية، وذلك يوجب القول بالجوهر الفرد. وأيضاً: فتلك المماسة المتعاقبة إنما تحصل في آنات متلاصقة. وهذا يوجب القول بتتالي الآنات. وهو الذي أردناه في هذا المقام. والله أعلم.
The fifth proof for the succession of instants: that we say: There is no doubt that the center of the epicycle is a point. So when the carrier orb moves, from the motion of the center of the epicycle a circle is traced, called in astronomy the 'circle carrying the epicycle's center', and that circle in all its parts becomes touched by that point. But nothing touches a point except a point. So since this point which is the center has touched all parts of that circle, and it is established that contact only occurs at a point, it must be concluded that that circle is composed of successive points, and that necessitates that a line is composed of contiguous points, and that necessitates affirming the indivisible substance (al-jawhar al-fard). Also, those successive contacts only occur in contiguous instants. And this necessitates affirming the succession of instants. That is what we intended in this context. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof for the succession of instants (تتالي الآنات) and also for the existence of indivisible substance (الجوهر الفرد). The argument uses an astronomical example: the center of an epicycle (مركز التدوير) is a point. As the carrier orb moves, this point traces a circle. Since the point touches every part of that circle, and a point can only be touched by another point, the entire circle must be composed of points—i.e., the circumference is formed by successive points. This leads to the conclusion that a line is composed of contiguous points (atomic parts of space). Furthermore, the successive contacts between the center point and the points of the circle occur in contiguous instants (آنات متلاصقة), proving the succession of instants. Thus, the proof simultaneously establishes atomism in space and discreteness in time.

Key Terms

نقطة
دائرة
مماسة
جوهر فرد
تتالي الآنات
آنات متلاصقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof requires actual physical contact in the celestial spheres, which is impossible because celestial spheres are incorporeal.
Correction: The proof is purely geometrical: 'contact' here means that the point coincides with each point of the circle in succession, not a physical collision. It is a mathematical argument about points and lines.

Checkpoint

A) A line is infinitely divisible.
B) A line is composed of contiguous points.
C) A line is composed of extended atoms.
D) A line has no real existence.

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof uses a geometrical argument with an epicycle to simultaneously establish the indivisible substance (atomism in space) and the succession of instants (atomism in time).

The Argument from Correspondence
Razi introduces the third inquiry and states the argument for atomism via correspondence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi argues that body is composed of indivisible parts by appealing to the correspondence between motion, time, and distance.

Core Idea
Body's composition mirrors the discrete nature of motion and time.

Razi continues his investigation into the nature of bodies by presenting the third inquiry. Building on earlier conclusions that motion and time are composed of indivisible units, he now extends this reasoning to the structure of body itself. The key is the principle of correspondence between motion, time, and distance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure
Notice that Razi begins by naming this the 'third inquiry' of the chapter. This frames the following as a distinct argument.
2
Understand the premises
The argument starts from the previously established ideas: motion is composed of successive indivisible parts, and time is composed of consecutive indivisible instants. These are taken as given.
3
Grasp the correspondence principle
Razi asserts that motion, time, and distance are three mutually corresponding things. This means their structures mirror each other.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since motion and time are discrete, distance (and hence body) must also be composed of indivisible parts. Note that Razi mentions this conclusion is agreed upon between theologians and philosophers.
The passage is cut off before the full demonstration is given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث من مطالب هذا الفصل: في بيان أنه لما كانت الحركة مركبة من أجزاء متعاقبة، كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة، وكان الزمان من آنات متتالية، كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة، وجب أن يكون الجسم مركباً من أجزاء لا يتجزأ كل واحد منها، ولا يقبل القسمة. واعلم: أن هذا الفصل كالمتفق عليه بيننا وبين الفلاسفة. فإن الكل اتفقوا على أن الحركة والزمان والمسافة: أمور ثلاثة متطابقة. فإن ثبت كون
The third type of inquiries of this chapter: concerning the demonstration that since motion is composed of successive parts, each of which is indivisible, and time is composed of consecutive instants, each of which is indivisible, it is necessary that body be composed of parts each of which is indivisible and does not accept division. And know: that this chapter is as if agreed upon between us and the philosophers. For all agreed that motion, time, and distance are three mutually corresponding things. For if it is established that...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage introduces the third inquiry of the chapter: proving that body (الجسم) is composed of indivisible parts (أجزاء لا تتجزأ). The argument is based on the previously established fact that motion is composed of successive indivisible parts and time is composed of consecutive indivisible instants. Since motion, time, and distance are mutually corresponding (مطابقة), the spatial distance traversed must also be composed of indivisible parts. The author notes that this conclusion is agreed upon between the theologians (mutakallimun) and the philosophers (الفلسفة), a rare point of consensus. However, the passage is cut off mid-sentence ('فإن ثبت كون'), so the full demonstration is not present.

The Argument from Saturn's Contact for Successive Moments
Argument from Saturn's contact to prove tatali al-anat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the contact of celestial spheres demonstrates the necessity of successive moments (tatali al-anat).

Core Idea
The contact of Saturn proves time is composed of discrete moments.

In this passage, the author presents a concise proof for the doctrine of tatali al-anat (succession of moments) using the example of Saturn's sphere contacting the fixed stars. By analyzing the logic, you will see how an impossibility (interruption of motions) leads to the conclusion that time is not continuous but consists of discrete instants.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice how the argument is structured as a conditional proof.
The passage has two parts: a brief conditional statement and then a more formal proof.
2
Identify the key moments
The argument hinges on two moments: the moment of contact between Saturn and the fixed stars, and the moment when that point is no longer in contact. Understand that both occur instantaneously.
These moments are the building blocks of the proof.
3
Follow the two possibilities
The author considers two cases: either there is a time interval between these two moments, or there is not. Trace the consequence of each case.
Pay attention to why the first case is deemed false.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since the first case leads to a false consequence (interruption of celestial motions), the second case must be true, which implies that moments follow one another without any time in between.
This conclusion establishes tatali al-anat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زمان السكون ، لزمكم انقطاع حركات الافلاك . وذلك عندكم باطل . وإن لم يحصل هناك سكون متخلل بين الأنين ، فحينئذ يلزم تتالي الآنات . وهو المطلوب . إذا عرفت هذا ، فنقول : إنا أردنا إيراد هذا الكلام في صورة البرهان قلنا : لا شك أن حصول الملاقاة . بين كرة ( زحل ، وبين الكرة المكوكبة ، تقع دفعة في آن . وصيرورة تلك النقطة لا ملاقية ولا مماسة ، تقع أيضاً في آن . فإن حصل بين الآن زمان ، يكون ( زحل ) فيه ساكناً ، لزم انقطاع حركات الكواكب. وهو باطل . وإن لم يحصل هناك هذا الزمان المتخلل ، فحينئذ يلزم تتالي الآنات . وهو المطلوب
If there were a time of rest, you would be required to have interruption of the motions of the celestial spheres. And that is false according to you. And if there is no rest interposed between the two moments, then necessarily follows the succession of moments. And that is the desired conclusion. Now that you know this, we say: We intended to present this statement in the form of a proof [and] we said: There is no doubt that the contact between the sphere of Saturn and the sphere of the fixed stars occurs instantaneously in a moment. And the becoming of that point neither contacting nor touching also occurs in a moment. Now if there is a time between the two moments, in which Saturn would be stationary, then it would necessitate the interruption of the motions of the celestial spheres. And that is false. And if this interposed time does not exist, then it necessitates the succession of moments. And that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) for the doctrine of tatali al-anat (succession of moments) using the example of Saturn's contact with the fixed stars. The author presents an argument in two parts: first a conditional reasoning, then a formal proof. The argument assumes that contact occurs in a moment. If there is a time interval between the moment of contact and the moment of separation, then Saturn would be stationary during that interval, which would interrupt its motion—an impossibility. Therefore, there is no interval, so the moments succeed each other without any time between them. This establishes the doctrine of unextended moments.

Key Terms
تتالي الآنات
زمان السكون
حركات الأفلاك
الملاقاة
الآنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the argument assumes continuous motion, but it actually uses contact instants to prove atomic time.
Correction: The argument does not assume continuity; it uses the occurrence of contact and separation in moments to show that any interval would require stationary time, which is impossible for celestial motions. Thus, time must be atomic (discrete moments).

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence if there were a time interval between the moment of contact and the moment of separation of Saturn?
A) Saturn would move faster
B) Saturn would be stationary, causing interruption of motions
C) The fixed stars would disappear
D) Nothing would happen

Key Takeaway
The contact of Saturn with the fixed stars proves that time consists of successive moments without any interval, establishing tatali al-anat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that between two moments there cannot be any interval of rest. In your own life, are there moments of spiritual 'rest'—periods of negligence or procrastination—that you allow to break your continuous devotion? ?

?
The contact of Saturn is instantaneous—there is no 'time' to hesitate. When you are faced with a choice between right and wrong, do you act immediately or do you let a 'gap' of hesitation allow temptation to creep in? What would change if you treated every moral moment as an indivisible atom demanding an instant response?

Fifth Proof: Epicycle Center and Successive Moments
Fifth proof using the epicycle center to prove lines are composed of points and moments are consecutive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the motion of the epicycle center is used to prove that lines are composed of indivisible points (jawhar fard) and that moments are consecutive (tatali al-anat).

Core Idea
The point of the epicycle shows space and time are made of atoms.

Sanusi now presents a fifth proof for the succession of moments, this time drawing from the astronomical model of epicycles. By analyzing the contact between a moving point and a circle, he argues that lines must be composed of points and moments must be consecutive. This lesson unpacks that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation to ensure you grasp the overall flow of the proof.
Notice that the proof uses a specific astronomical concept: the epicycle's center.
2
Trace the logical steps
Identify the key reasoning: the center is a point; its motion traces a circle; only a point can touch a point; therefore the circle is made of points; this implies the line is made of points, hence the indivisible atom. Then the same logic yields contiguous moments.
This proof simultaneously establishes spatial and temporal atoms.
3
Reflect on the dual conclusion
Consider why Sanusi explicitly mentions both the indivisible atom and the succession of moments. How does the argument for moments mirror the argument for points?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة في إثبات تتالي الآنات : أن نقول : لا شك أن مركز كـرة التدوير نقطة . فإذا تحرك الفلك الحامل، فإنه يرتسم من حركة مركز التدوير دائرة ، تسمي في علم الهيئة بـ ( الدائرة الحاملة لمركز التدوير ، وتلك الدائرة بجميع أجزائها ، صارت ممسوسة لتلك النقطة . لكن النقطة لا يماسها إلا نقطة ، فلما كانت هذه النقطة التي هي المركز ، قد مست بجميع أجزاء تلك الدائرة ، وثبت أن المماسة ما حصلت إلا على النقطة ، وجب القطع بأن تلك الدائرة مرتسمة من النقط المتوالية ، وذلك يقتضي كون الخط مركبا من النقط المتلاقية ، وذلك يوجب القول بالجوهر الفرد، وأيضاً : فتلك المماسة المتعاقبة إنما تحصل في آنات متلاصقة . وهذا يوجب القول بتالي الآنات . وهو الذي أردناه في هذا المقام . والله أعلم .
The fifth proof for the succession of moments: That we say: There is no doubt that the center of the epicycle sphere is a point. So when the deferent sphere moves, from the motion of the center of the epicycle a circle is traced, called in astronomy 'the deferent circle of the center of the epicycle', and that circle in all its parts becomes touched by that point. But only a point can touch a point. So when this point, which is the center, has touched all parts of that circle, and it is established that touching only occurred on the point, it must be determined that that circle is composed of successive points, and that necessitates that the line is composed of contiguous points, and that necessitates the assertion of the indivisible atom. And also: those successive touchings occur only in contiguous moments. And this necessitates the assertion of the succession of moments. And that is what we intended in this context. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth explicit proof (al-hujjah al-khamisah) for the same doctrine, but using the epicycle model. The center of the epicycle is a point. As the deferent moves, it traces a circle. Since only a point can touch a point, and the center touches all parts of the circle, the circle must be composed of successive points, which means the line is composed of points, implying atoms (jawhar fard). Additionally, the successive touchings occur in contiguous moments (anat mutala-siqah), which proves the succession of moments (tatali al-anat). Thus both atomic spatial units and atomic temporal units are established.

مركز التدوير
الدائرة الحاملة
المماسة
النقط المتوالية
الجوهر الفرد
آنات متلاصقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof only deals with spatial atoms (jawhar fard).
Correction: The proof explicitly extends to temporal atoms: the successive touchings occur in contiguous moments, establishing the succession of moments (tatali al-anat).

Checkpoint
What is the circle traced by the center of the epicycle called?
A) The deferent circle of the center of the epicycle
B) The epicyclic circle
C) The eccentric circle
D) The equator

Key Takeaway
This proof uses the epicycle's center to argue for both atomic space (jawhar fard) and successive moments (tatali al-anat).

?
The center point touches the entire circle only because the circle is made of points. Consider your own actions: are they discrete deeds each accountable before Allah, or do you see them as a continuous flow that escapes sincerity? How can you make each 'point' of your life intentional worship?

The Correspondence Proof for Atomism
Proof that body is composed of indivisible parts because motion and time are composed of such parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the kalam argument uses the correspondence between motion, time, and distance to prove that body is composed of indivisible particles (atoms).

Core Idea
If motion and time are made of indivisible steps, so must distance be.

In this passage, the author presents a third type of argument for atomism, building on the agreed premise that motion, time, and distance are parallel. He then gives a rigorous proof by contradiction: if the distance corresponding to an indivisible unit of motion were divisible, then motion and time would also be divisible, contradicting the assumption. Thus the distance must be indivisible, yielding atoms for body.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the claim: because motion and time are composed of indivisible parts, body must be composed of atoms.
The passage is a proof, so pay attention to the logical structure.
2
Understand the agreed premise
The author states that motion, time, and distance are mutually conforming. This means if one is composed of indivisible parts, all are. This premise is agreed upon with philosophers.
This premise is crucial for the proof.
3
Follow the proof by contradiction
The proof considers a specific amount of distance traversed by an indivisible motion in an indivisible time. It asks whether that distance is divisible or not. If divisible, motion and time would also be divisible, contradicting the assumption. So it must be indivisible, i.e., an atom.
This shows the indivisibility of distance directly.
4
Connect to atomism
Since each indivisible part of motion and time corresponds to an indivisible part of distance, the entire distance (and thus the body) is composed of such atoms.
This completes the proof that body is made of indivisible parts.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and consider the common misunderstanding to solidify your grasp of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث من مطالب هذا الفصل : في بيان أنه لما كانت الحـركـة مركبة من أجزاء متعاقبة ، كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة ، وكان الزمان من آنات متتالية ، كل واحد منها لا يقبل القسمة ، وجب أن يكون الجسم مركباً من أجزاء لا يتجزأ كل واحد منها ، ولا يقبل القسمة

واعلم : أن هذا الفصل كالمتفق عليه بيننا وبين الفلاسفة . فإن الكل اتفقوا على أن الحركة والزمان والمسافة : أمور ثلاثة متطابقة . فإن ثبت كون واحد منها مركباً من أجزاء لا تتجزأ ، كان الحال في الكل كذلك . وإذا كانت هذه المقدمة ، مقدمة اتفاقية . فلا حاجة بنا إلى تقريرها بالبرهان . إلا أنا نبين البرهان القاطع على صحتها ، مبالغة في البيان والتقدير . فنقول : الدليل عليه : هو أن المقدار المعين من المسافة الذي يتحرك المتحرك عليه ، بالجزء الذي لا يتجزأ من الحبركة ، في الآن الذي لا ينقسم من الزمان . إما أن يكون منقسماً أو لا يكون منقسماً فإن كان منقسماً كانت الحركة إلى نصفه توجد قبل الحركة من نصفه إلى آخره . فتكون تلك الحركة منقسمة . وقد فرضناها غير منقسمة . وأيضاً : الزمان الذي يقع في النصف الأول من الحركة ، متقدماً على الزمان الذي فيه النصف الثاني . فيكون ذلك الآن منقسماً . وقد فرضناه غير منقسم . هذا خلف . وأما إن كان ذلك المقدار المعين من المسافة غير منقسم . فهو الجوهر الفرد . ثم بهذا الطريق يقع كل واحد من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ من الحركة، وكل واحد من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزىء من الزمان ، في مقابلة جزء لا يتجزأ من المسافة . وذلك يقتضي كون المسافة مركبة من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ وذلك هو المطلوب . والله ولي التوفيق والإحسان
The third type of the demands of this chapter: In explaining that since motion is composed of successive parts, each one of which is indivisible, and time is composed of successive moments, each one of which is indivisible, then it is necessary that the body is composed of parts each one of which is indivisible and admits no division.

And know that this chapter is as if agreed upon between us and the philosophers. For all agreed that motion, time, and distance are three mutually conforming things. For if it is established that one of them is composed of indivisible parts, then the situation is the same for all. And since this premise is an agreed premise, we have no need to establish it by proof. But we present the decisive proof of its correctness, for the sake of thoroughness in explanation and presentation. So we say: The proof for it is that the specific amount of distance over which the moving thing moves with the indivisible part of motion [al-harakah?], in the indivisible moment of time, is either divisible or not divisible. If it is divisible, then the motion to its half occurs before the motion from its half to the end. So that motion becomes divided, while we had assumed it to be undivided. Also: the time that occurs in the first half of the motion is prior to the time in which the second half occurs. So that moment becomes divided, while we had assumed it to be undivided. This is a contradiction. And if that specific amount of distance is indivisible, then it is the indivisible atom. Then in this way each one of the indivisible parts of motion and each one of the indivisible parts of time corresponds to an indivisible part of distance. And that necessitates that the distance is composed of indivisible parts. And that is the desired conclusion. And God is the giver of success and beneficence.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a third type of argument (al-naw' al-thalith) concerning the necessary composition of body from indivisible parts given the nature of motion and time. The author first states the agreed-upon principle that motion, time, and distance correspond. Then he provides a decisive proof: when a moving object moves over a certain distance with an indivisible unit of motion in an indivisible unit of time, the corresponding distance must be either divisible or not. If divisible, the motion and time would also be divisible, contradicting the assumption. Therefore, the distance must be indivisible, i.e., an atom. Thus each indivisible part of motion and time corresponds to an indivisible part of distance, proving that the entire distance (and hence body) is composed of atoms.

Key Terms
الحركة
الزمان
المسافة
الجوهر الفرد
الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ
المقدار المعين
الخلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument assumes the indivisibility of motion and time and then deduces the same for distance.
Correction: Actually, the argument assumes the indivisibility of motion and time as a premise (or as something already proven) and uses the correspondence to prove that distance must also be indivisible. It does not assume the conclusion about distance.

Checkpoint

A) Motion would remain indivisible
B) Both motion and time would become divisible, contradicting the assumption
C) The distance would become infinite
D) The atom would be confirmed

Key Takeaway
The correspondence between motion, time, and distance forces distance to be composed of indivisible parts, proving atomism.

Proof from Motion for the Indivisible Atom
Sanusi presents a proof by contradiction from motion and time for the indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's proof by contradiction that establishes the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) based on the indivisibility of motion and time.

Core Idea
If motion and time are indivisible, then space must also be indivisible.

Sanusi presents a powerful proof from motion for the existence of the indivisible atom. He uses a logical argument that if a moving object covers a distance in an indivisible motion and time, then that distance itself must be indivisible. This refutes the idea of infinite divisibility of space.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
Sanusi begins by noting that if a whole is composed of indivisible parts, then each part is likewise. He says this premise is agreed upon but will prove it decisively.
2
Follow the proof by contradiction
Consider a specific distance covered by one indivisible motion in one indivisible moment. Assume the distance is divisible. Then the motion and time become divisible, contradicting the assumption. Therefore the distance must be indivisible.
Trace the two branches: divisible leads to contradiction; indivisible leads to the atom.
3
Recognize the conclusion
The indivisible distance is the atom. Consequently, all parts of motion and time correspond to indivisible parts of distance, proving that space is composed of such parts.
This completes the proof for the indivisible atom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد منها مركباً من أجزاء لا تتجزأ ، كان الحال في الكل كذلك . وإذا كانت هذه المقدمة ، مقدمة اتفاقية . فلا حاجة بنا إلى تقريرها بالبرهان . إلا أنا نبين البرهان القاطع على صحتها ، مبالغة في البيان والتقدير . فنقول : الدليل عليه : هو أن المقدار المعين من المسافة الذي يتحرك المتحرك عليه ، بالجزء الذي لا يتجزأ من الحركة ، في الآن الذي لا ينقسم من الزمان . إما أن يكون منقسماً أو لا يكون منقسماً فإن كان منقسماً كانت الحركة إلى نصفه توجد قبل الحركة من نصفه إلى آخره . فتكون تلك الحركة منقسمة . وقد فرضناها غير منقسمة . وأيضاً : الزمان الذي يقع في النصف الأول من الحركة ، متقدماً على الزمان الذي فيه النصف الثاني . فيكون ذلك الآن منقسماً . وقد فرضناه غير منقسم . هذا خلف . وأما إن كان ذلك المقدار المعين من المسافة غير منقسم . فهو الجوهر الفرد . ثم بهذا الطريق يقع كل واحد من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ من الحركة، وكل واحد من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ من الزمان ، في مقابلة جزء لا يتجزأ من المسافة . وذلك يقتضي كون المسافة مركبة من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ وذلك هو المطلوب . والله ولي التوفيق والإحسان
One of them is composed of parts that are indivisible, so the situation for the whole is likewise. And since this premise is an agreed-upon premise, we have no need to establish it by proof, except that we will show the decisive proof of its correctness, out of elaboration in explanation and estimation. So we say: The proof for it is that the specific measure of distance which the moving thing moves across, by the indivisible part of motion, in the indivisible moment of time, is either divisible or not divisible. If it is divisible, then the motion to its half occurs before the motion from its half to its end, so that motion becomes divisible, whereas we assumed it indivisible. Also, the time that occurs in the first half of the motion precedes the time in which the second half occurs, so that moment becomes divisible, whereas we assumed it indivisible. This is a contradiction. But if that specific measure of distance is indivisible, then it is the indivisible atom. Then in this way, each one of the indivisible parts of motion and each one of the indivisible parts of time corresponds to an indivisible part of distance. And that necessitates that the distance be composed of parts that are indivisible, and that is what was desired. And God is the Grantor of success and beneficence.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a proof by contradiction (burhan khalfi) for the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The author begins by noting that if a whole is composed of indivisible parts, then any part of it is likewise composed of indivisible parts. He says that this premise is agreed upon, so he could simply rely on it, but he provides a decisive proof for elaboration. The proof: Consider a specific distance that a moving object traverses using one indivisible part of motion in one indivisible moment of time. This distance is either divisible or not. If it is divisible, then the motion to its halfway point occurs before the motion from the halfway point to the end, meaning that motion is divisible (contrary to our assumption). The same applies to time: the time for the first half precedes the time for the second half, making the moment divisible. This yields a contradiction. Therefore, the distance must be indivisible, and that indivisible distance is the atom (al-jawhar al-fard). Consequently, all parts of motion and time correspond to indivisible parts of distance, proving that distance is composed of such parts. This is the desired conclusion.

الحركة (al-harakah)
الزمان (al-zaman)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof assumes the existence of indivisible parts from the start.
Correction: The proof does not assume it; it deduces the indivisibility of distance from the indivisibility of motion and time via contradiction.

Geometric Proof of the Indivisible Atom: Sphere and Plane
First geometric proof for the indivisible atom using sphere and plane contact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first geometric proof for the indivisible atom based on the contact between a sphere and a plane.

Core Idea
The point of contact between a sphere and a plane must be indivisible.

This lesson examines a key argument from classical Islamic theology that uses geometry to prove the existence of indivisible atoms (al-jawhar al-fard). The argument shows that when a perfect sphere touches a flat surface, the point of contact cannot be divided, otherwise contradictions arise. We will work through the first two aspects of this proof, though the second is incomplete in the source.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setup
Recognize that the proof concerns a 'true sphere' (al-kurah al-haqiqiyyah) and a plane surface, and the claim that their contact point is indivisible.
2
Analyze the first face
Read the first argument: if the contact point were divisible, it would coincide with the plane (making part of the sphere flat), which is impossible. Also consider the rolling sphere scenario.
Notice the two sub-parts: the coincidence argument and the rolling argument.
3
Identify the second face (incomplete)
Read the beginning of the second face, which is cut off. Understand that the proof originally had four aspects, but only these are preserved.
The second face likely continued a similar reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this geometric reasoning supports the existence of indivisible atoms in Islamic kalam. The contact point's indivisibility implies a fundamental physical unit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الخا المسألة الحالة على إثبات الجوهر الفرد المستنبطة من الأصول الهندسية الحجة الأولى : إن الكرة الحقيقية إذا لقيت سطحاً مستوياً ، كان موضع الملاقاة شيئاً غير منقسم . وذلك يوجب القول بإثبات الجوهر الفرد . أما بيان أن موضع الملاقاة غير منقسم فلوجوه أربعة : الأول : إن موضع الملاقاة لو كان منقسماً لكان ذلك الموضع منطبقاً على السطح المستوي . والمنطبق على السطح المستوي سطح مستوي ، فيلزم أن يحصل في الكرة سطح مستوي . وذلك محال . وأيضاً : فإذا فرضنا أن تلك الكرة تدحرجت ، فعند زوال تلك المماسة ، تحصل المماسة بجزء آخر غير منقسم أيضاً . فالجزء الثاني الذي حصلت المماسة الثانية به . إما أن يحصل بالجزء الأول الذي حصلت المماسة الأولى على زاوية ، أو لا على زاوية ، صارت الكرة جسماً ممتداً على الاستقامة . وذلك محال . الوجه الثاني في بيان أن موضع الملاقاة غير منقسم : هو أنه لو كان
Chapter [the fifth?] The current issue on the proof of the indivisible atom derived from geometrical principles. The first argument: That if a true sphere meets a plane surface, the place of contact is an indivisible thing. And that necessitates asserting the indivisible atom. As for the demonstration that the place of contact is indivisible, it has four aspects: The first: If the place of contact were divisible, then that place would coincide with the plane surface, and what coincides with a plane surface is a plane surface, so it would entail that there be a plane surface in the sphere, and that is impossible. Also, if we suppose that sphere rolls, then upon the removal of that tangency, tangency occurs at another indivisible part as well. So the second part by which the second tangency occurs: either it occurs at an angle with the first part by which the first tangency occurred, or not at an angle, [then] the sphere would become a body extended in a straight line, and that is impossible. The second aspect in demonstrating that the place of contact is indivisible: that if it were ... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents the first geometric proof for the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The author states that when a true sphere (al-kurah al-haqiqiyyah) touches a plane surface, the point of contact must be indivisible. This is supported by four aspects (wujuh). The first aspect: if the contact point were divisible, it would coincide with the plane surface, meaning a portion of the sphere would be flat — impossible for a perfect sphere. Moreover, if the sphere rolls, the new contact point would be another indivisible part. This second contact must either be at an angle to the first or not; if not at an angle, the sphere would be a straight line (since all contacts would lie on a line), which is also impossible. The second aspect begins but is cut off; it likely continues the argument from another angle.

الكرة الحقيقية
سطح مستوي
موضع الملاقاة
مماسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sphere's contact point is a mathematical point with no extension, so divisibility is irrelevant.
Correction: The argument concerns physical indivisibility, not mathematical points. In kalam, atoms are physical, not just ideal.

Key Takeaway
The indivisibility of the contact point between a sphere and a plane serves as a geometric proof for the existence of indivisible atoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Are you treating each moment as indivisible and decisive, or are you allowing compromises that stretch your resolve into a straight line of inconsistency? What one point can you commit to today?
?
The impossibility of a flat surface on a perfect sphere mirrors the impossibility of any imperfection in the Creator. If even a geometric sphere cannot have a flat part, how much more must Allah be free from any deficiency? How does this truth affect your understanding of Tawhid and your reliance on Him as absolutely perfect?

Two Responses to the Objection About the Place of Contact
The author gives two responses to the objection that the place of contact is non-existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two responses to the objection that the place of contact is non-existent, and why the point is considered an existing entity.

Core Idea
The place of contact is real; denying it leads to absurdity.

This short passage presents a swift rebuttal to a skeptical objection. The objector claims the place where two things meet is not an existing thing. The author responds with two clear arguments: first, the objector's own system identifies it as the point, which exists; second, if it were non-existent, the thing making contact would be nothing at all. Both responses uphold the reality of contact.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector says the place of contact is not an existing thing. This would undermine the reality of physical contact.
2
Analyze the first response
The first response turns the objector's own premises against them: they accept the point as a real entity, and the point is precisely the place of contact.
3
Analyze the second response
The second response shows the logical consequence: if the place were non-existent, then the thing contacting would be described as contacting nothing, making it pure non-existence, which is impossible.
4
Reflect on the strength of the responses
Notice how the author uses both internal consistency (first) and logical impossibility (second) to defeat the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجهين : قوله : « لا نسلم أن موضع الملاقاة أمر موجود ، قلنا : الجواب عنه من وجهين : الأول : إن موضع الملاقاة عندكم ، هو النقطة . وهي أمر موجود والثاني : إنه لو لم يكن موجوداً ، لكان الموصوف بالملاقاة عدماً محضاً ، وإنه محال .
Two aspects: He said: 'We do not accept that the place of contact is an existing thing.' We said: The answer to it is from two aspects: The first: The place of contact according to you is the point, and it is an existing thing. And the second: If it were non-existent, then what is described by contact would be pure non-existence, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents two responses to an objection. The objector denies that the place of contact is an existing entity. The author answers from two angles. First, the objector's own position (that of the proponents of atomism) holds that the place of contact is the point, and the point is an existing thing. Second, if the place of contact were non-existent, then the thing that is described as making contact would be pure nothingness, which is impossible. Thus the place of contact must exist.

Key Terms
ملاقاة
نقطة
عدماً محضاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The point is not a real entity, so the place of contact is non-existent.
Correction: In the atomist view, the point is an existing entity, so the place of contact is real.

Checkpoint

B) The place of contact is a line.

Key Takeaway
The place of contact is real; the point is an existing entity, and denying its existence leads to logical absurdity.

?

How does this logical argument train your mind to be more rigorous in matters of faith? Write down one area where you need to apply the same logical consistency.

Responding to the Sphere Objection
The author responds to the objection that spheres prevent atomism by showing they require atoms and sliding proves it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends atomism against the objection that spheres and circles are incompatible with it.

Core Idea
Spheres and circles actually prove atomism — even if they slide.

This lesson tackles a key objection: if spheres and circles exist, how can atoms be real? The author shows the objection fails because spheres necessitate atoms, and even if rolling is impossible, sliding works just as well to prove atomism. Let's see the logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the dialectical structure: objection, reply, sub-objection, reply.
2
Identify the two objections
The first objection says spheres prevent atomism. The second objects that spheres cannot roll. See how the author responds to each.
3
Understand the sliding argument
Even if rolling is impossible, sliding on a plane still creates a line composed of points of contact, which supports atomism. This is the key move.
Think about how points of contact imply indivisible units (atoms).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : « القول بإثبات الكرة والدائرة ، يمنع من إثبات الجوهر الفرد ، قلنا : لا نسلم . فإننا قد دللنا على أن ذلك يوجب الجوهر الفرد ، قوله : « لا نسلم إمكان تدحرج الكرة ، قلنا : هب أنه لا يصح تدحرجها ، لكن لا نزاع في إمكان انزلاقها، على السطح المستوي. وبتقدير انزلاقها ، فإنه يفترض في البسيط خط مركب من نقط التماس ، ويحصل المقصود .
He said: 'The assertion of the sphere and circle prevents the affirmation of the atom (al-jawhar al-fard).' We said: We do not accept that. For we have demonstrated that that necessitates the atom. He said: 'We do not accept the possibility of the sphere rolling.' We said: Even if its rolling is not valid, there is no dispute about the possibility of its sliding on a plane surface. And assuming its sliding, then a line composed of points of contact is assumed in the simple surface, and the intended result is obtained.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage addresses a new objection: that if we affirm the existence of spheres and circles, that would prevent the proof of atomism. The author first rejects the objection outright, stating that they have already demonstrated that the sphere and circle actually require the atom. Then a sub-objection is raised: the sphere cannot roll (which would be necessary for the previous proof). The author responds by conceding that rolling may be invalid, but that sliding is possible and uncontested. Under sliding, the sphere's contact with the plane generates a line composed of points of contact, thus proving atomism.

Key Terms
الكرة (sphere)
الدائرة (circle)
الجوهر الفرد (atom)
التدحرج (rolling)
الانزلاق (sliding)
نقط التماس (points of contact)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that rolling is essential for the sphere to prove atomism.
Correction: Rolling is not necessary; sliding alone generates points of contact that confirm atomism.

Checkpoint

A) Rolling is possible.
B) Rolling is impossible, but sliding is possible.
C) Both rolling and sliding are impossible.
D) The sphere does not need to move.

Key Takeaway
The sphere objection does not refute atomism; rather, spheres require atoms, and sliding provides the necessary proof.

What one change will you make today to be more intentional in your smallest interactions?
?
The author uses sliding to prove atomism. Refuting the Line-Contact Objection: Why a Sphere Touches at a Point
Refutation of the claim that a sphere touches a plane with a line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a sphere cannot touch a plane surface with a line, based on the necessary condition of coincidence in contact (tamās).

Core Idea
Contact requires coincidence, and a line on a sphere cannot coincide with a straight line.

This passage tackles a subtle objection against the atomist view of contact. If a sphere touches a plane with a line, then that line on the sphere would have to exactly coincide with a straight line on the plane. But the author shows this leads to an impossibility, thereby confirming that contact must occur at a point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the response
Start by reading the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author begins by stating the objection ('the sphere touches with a line') and then responds with 'We said: This is absolutely false...'
The passage is a single continuous argument, so read it as a whole before analyzing.
2
Understand the key term: coincidence (انطباق)
The author defines contact (mumāssa) as requiring coincidence (inṭibāq) of one touching thing upon the other. This is a crucial premise: contact isn't just proximity but exact alignment.
In classical kalām, contact is analyzed geometrically, not just physically.
3
Follow the logical chain of the argument
The author argues: If the sphere touches with a line, then that line must coincide with a straight line on the plane. But what coincides with a straight line is itself straight. Therefore, the sphere's circumference would have a straight line, which is impossible. Conclusion: the original claim is false.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: assuming the objection leads to an absurdity.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
This argument supports the atomist position that contact occurs at a point, not a line or surface. It shows how careful geometric reasoning underpins kalām discussions of bodies and accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( الكرة حال تدحرجها تماس السطح المستوي بالخط ، قلنا : هذا باطل قطعاً ، لأن المماسة لا تحصل إلا بانطباق أحد المماسين على الآخر ، فلو ماست الكرة السطح بالخط ، لحصل في الكرة خط منطبق على الخط المستقيم ، المرتسم في السطح المستوي. والمنطبق على المستقيم مستقيم . فيلزم أن يحصل على محيط الكرة ، خط مستقيم . وذلك باطل
He said: 'The sphere while rolling touches the plane surface with a line.' We said: This is absolutely false, because contact does not occur except by the coincidence of one of the two contacting things upon the other. So if the sphere were to touch the surface with a line, then there would occur in the sphere a line coinciding with the straight line that is drawn on the plane surface. And that which coincides with a straight line is straight. Consequently, a straight line would occur on the circumference of the sphere. And that is false.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection that the sphere touches the plane with a line rather than a point. The author argues that contact requires one thing to exactly coincide with the other. If the sphere touched with a line, that line on the sphere would have to coincide with a straight line on the plane. But anything coinciding with a straight line is itself straight. This would imply that the sphere's circumference contains a straight line, which is impossible for a sphere. Therefore, the sphere cannot touch with a line, supporting the atomist view that contact is at a point.

Key Terms
المماسة (contact/tangency)
الانطباق (coincidence)
الخط المستقيم (straight line)
محيط الكرة (circumference of the sphere)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A sphere can touch a plane surface along a line (like a line of contact).
Correction: The author proves this leads to a contradiction: the sphere's circumference would have to contain a straight line, which is geometrically impossible. Contact must be at a point.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the claim that the sphere touches with a line to be false?
A) Because contact requires coincidence, and a line on the sphere would be straight.
B) Because the sphere cannot roll.
C) Because the plane is not straight.
D) Because the sphere is not a circle.

Key Takeaway
Contact (mumāssa) requires coincidence (inṭibāq), so a sphere cannot touch a plane with a line without producing an absurd straight line on its circumference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you assume something small (like a sphere touching with a line), do you ever ignore where it logically leads? Are you willing to follow your assumptions to their absurd conclusions, even if they seem harmless at first?
?
This argument shows that a single false premise can force a contradiction. Have you ever held a belief about Allah's attributes that, if followed strictly, leads to an impossibility? What will you do about it?
?
The author could have just said 'it's false,' but he proved it with clear reasoning. When you encounter doubts about your faith, do you demand solid proofs, or do you settle for emotional comfort? How will you train yourself to think like the scholars who refuted falsehood with logic?

Defending Line Composition from Sphere Contacts
The author refutes the objection that a sphere's single contact prevents line formation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author of Al-Matalibul Aliyah defends the composition of a line from indivisible points against the objection that a sphere always has only one point of contact.

Core Idea
Successive contacts in atomic time allow a line to be composed of indivisible points.

The objection claims that if a sphere always has only one point of contact at any instant, then only that single point exists, making it impossible to derive a line composed of points. The author responds by positing a finite line on the sphere and explaining how successive contacts in distinct instants generate the adjacency of points, ultimately showing that the line drawn on a plane is composed of points.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening objection: if the sphere always has only one point of contact, then only one point exists at any time, so no line can be formed.
This is the challenge the author must overcome.
2
Follow the first response
The author posits that a finite line can exist on the sphere in actuality. The sphere meets the surface at a point, and when contact is removed, it meets at the next point. The first point remains as the line's endpoint.
Notice how this introduces a second point while maintaining the principle of non-adjacency.
3
Examine the time argument
The author concedes that two points are not adjacent in space, but argues the two contacts occur in two distinct instants. This leads to a succession of instants, which causes points to become adjacent in a temporal sense.
This is the key move: using atomic time to resolve spatial non-adjacency.
4
Conclude the argument
The line on the plane is formed by successive contacts of the indivisible point, so the line is composed of points. This is the desired result.
The argument shows that lines can be composed of points if time is atomic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : « الموجود في الكرة أبداً ، مماسة واحدة ، فالموجود فيها أبداً نقطة واحدة ، قلنا : يحتمل أن يحصل في الكرة خط ذو نهاية ، بالفعل ، ثم إن الكرة لقيت ذلك السطح بتلك النقطة ، ثم عند زوال الملاقاة عنها ، تحصل الملاقاة بنقطة أخرى تتلوها . فالنقطة الأولى تكون باقية بسبب كونها نهاية بالفعل لذلك الخط ، والنقطة الثانية تكون موجودة بسبب حصول المماسة عليها ، وحينئذ يحصل المطلوب . سلمنا : أنه لا يتشافع نقطتان ، لكن هاتان المماستان لا تحدثان إلا في آنين . فيلزم منه تتالي الآنات ، ومن تالي الآنات تتشافع النقط . وأيضاً : فالخط المرتسم على السطح المستوي ، إنما ارتسم من المماسات الحاصلة بالنقطة التي لا تتجزا ، فيكون ذلك الخط مؤلفاً من النقط وهو المطلوب
He said: 'What exists in the sphere is always one single contact, so what exists in it is always one point.' We said: It is possible that there occurs in the sphere an actually finite line, then the sphere meets that surface at that point, then when contact is removed from it, contact occurs at another point following it. So the first point remains due to its being an actual end of that line, and the second point exists due to the occurrence of contact upon it. And then the desired result is obtained. We concede that two points are not adjacent (yataschaffa'ān), but these two contacts do not occur except in two instants (ānayn). So from that follows the succession of instants, and from the succession of instants, points become adjacent. Also: the line drawn on the plane surface is only drawn from the contacts occurring by the indivisible point, so that line is composed of points, and that is the desired result.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that the sphere always has only one point of contact at any time, which would prevent the derivation of a line composed of points. The author replies by positing a finite line on the sphere that ends at the point of contact. When the sphere moves, contact shifts to the next point, and the first point remains as the line's endpoint. Thus two points exist simultaneously. Then the author concedes that points are not adjacent (a key atomist principle), but argues that the two contacts occur in two distinct instants. Since time is composed of successive indivisible instants, the points become adjacent in the sense of successive positions. Finally, the line on the plane is formed by successive contacts with the indivisible point, thus it is composed of points.

Key Terms
مماسة واحدة (single contact)
خط ذو نهاية (finite line)
نقطة لا تتجزا (indivisible point)
تتالي الآنات (succession of instants)
تشافع النقط (adjacency of points)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Points cannot become adjacent in any way, so a line cannot be composed of points.
Correction: While points are not spatially adjacent, they become adjacent through the succession of instants in atomic time.

Checkpoint
How does the author explain that points become adjacent despite the principle that two points are not adjacent?
A) By conceding that points are adjacent after all.
B) By arguing that the two contacts occur in two different instants, leading to succession of instants and hence adjacency.
C) By denying that the sphere moves.
D) By claiming that the line is not composed of points.

Key Takeaway
The author demonstrates that atomic time allows the composition of a line from points despite the spatial non-adjacency of points.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author argues that a line is composed of points through successive contacts in time. Your life is a line of actions across time. Each moment is a point of contact with the world. Are you aware of these moments, or do you let them blur into a vague continuity? How can you be more intentional about each 'point' of your day, knowing that each moment adds to the composition of your life?
?
The opponent thought that only one point could exist at a time, denying the possibility of a line. In your own life, do you ever feel that only one thing is possible at a time, missing the bigger picture of how discrete events string together to form a meaningful whole? What might you be overlooking because you are focused only on the present point?
?
If time is made of indivisible instants, each instant is a separate gift from Allah. How often do you treat each moment as precious and accountable? What would change if you truly believed that every instant is a discrete creation from Allah, not just a blur of continuous time?

Two Answers to the Objection that No Line Exists Between Two Contact Points
The author gives two ways to show that a line must exist between two contact points.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two ways the author argues that a line must exist between two contact points, and why denying it leads to the false doctrine of the leap.

Core Idea
There must be a line between contact points; otherwise points become adjacent or require a leap.

This passage addresses a key objection to the idea that a line is composed of points. The objector claims no line exists between two contact points. The author gives two arguments to show that a line must exist, and that the only alternative leads to an absurdity known as al-ṭafra (the leap).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a very compressed argumentative style.
2
Identify the two aspects
The passage says 'تقريره من وجهين' — its exposition is from two aspects. Find these two parts and see how they are structured.
The first aspect deals with the nature of what lies between two points; the second deals with the implications for contact.
3
Analyze the first aspect
The first aspect presents a dichotomy: between the two points there is either a point or a line. Consider each possibility and its consequence.
If a point, then points become adjacent (تشافع النقط). If a line, then we move to the second aspect.
4
Analyze the second aspect
Within the line option, the author presents another dichotomy: either the sphere touches the surface along that line or it does not. Trace the consequences of each.
If it does touch, the contact would be divisible. If it does not, that implies the leap (الطفرة).
5
Understand the conclusion
Both chords of the line option lead to falsehood (the divisibility issue and the leap). The author concludes that the objector's denial of a line is untenable.
The only remaining possibility from the first aspect is that points are adjacent, but that also contradicts the objector's position. Thus the existence of a line is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : لم قلتم : إنه لم يحصل بين تينك النقطتين خط ؟ قلنا : تقريره من وجهين : الأول : إن هاتين النقطتين ، إما أن يتخللهما نقطة أو خط . فإن كان الأول فقد حصل تشافع النقط . وإن كان الثاني ، فإما أن يقال : الكرة ماست السطح بذلك المستقيم ، أو لم تحصل المماسة على ذلك المستقيم . والأول باطل . وإلا لعاد ما ذكرنا من أن موضع المماسة يكون منقسماً . والثاني باطل · وإلا لزم أن يقال : الكرة ماست السطح بالنقطة الأولى ، ثم ماسته بالنقطة الثانية ، مع أنه لم تحصل المماسة بما بينهما . وذلك هو القول بالطفرة . وإنه باطل
He said: 'Why do you claim that a line has not occurred between those two points?' We said: Its exposition is from two aspects: The first: These two points, either a point or a line intervenes between them. If the first, then adjacency of points occurs. If the second, then either it is said that the sphere touched the surface along that straight line, or contact did not occur along that straight line. The first is false, otherwise what we mentioned returns, that the place of contact would be divisible. The second is false; otherwise it would necessitate saying that the sphere touched the surface at the first point, then touched it at the second point, while contact did not occur between them. That is the doctrine of the leap (al-ṭafra), and it is false.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage answers an objection that there is no line between the two contact points. The author presents two arguments. First, between the two points there must be either a point or a line. If a point, then points are adjacent (which contradicts atomist principles? Actually here the author is showing that if the objector denies a line, then the only alternative is a point, but that implies adjacency which the objector might accept as part of the proof; the author then shows the other option leads to a problem). If it is a line, then either the sphere touched the surface along that entire line or it did not. If it did, then the place of contact would be divisible (since a line is divisible), contradicting the atomist claim that contact is at an indivisible point. If it did not, then the sphere would have to 'jump' from the first point to the second without contacting the intermediate line, which is the doctrine of al-ṭafra (the leap), which the author deems false on Aristotelian grounds (since motion is continuous). Thus the only consistent alternative is that points are adjacent, supporting the composition of the line from points.

Key Terms
تشافع النقط (adjacency of points)
الطفرة (the leap)
المماسة (contact)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for two points to be in contact without a line between them.
Correction: The author proves that between any two points in contact, there must be a line, otherwise points would be adjacent (which leads to other issues) or involve a leap (which is false).

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the possibility of the sphere not contacting the line between two points?
A) It is acceptable because the sphere can jump.
B) It is the doctrine of the leap (al-ṭafra) and is false.
C) It leads to infinite points.
D) It is impossible because the sphere is round.

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the objection by showing that denying a line between contact points leads either to point adjacency or the absurdity of the leap.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever embraced a 'leap' in your spiritual life — expecting to reach a high state without passing through the gradual steps of worship and self-discipline? How does this passage's refutation of the leap call you to embrace the process that Allah has ordained?
?
When you face doubts, do you try to jump directly to certainty without patiently working through the intermediate steps of learning and reflection? What would it look like for you to honor the 'line' between points in your journey of faith?
?
The objector denies the line between points — are there areas where you deny the necessary connections between your actions and their outcomes, as if things can happen without cause? How can you live more consistently with the order Allah has placed in creation?

The Second Way: Instantaneous Contact and Adjacency
Second argument for successive contact points leading to adjacency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second kalam argument for the necessity of adjacency between successive points of contact in motion.

Core Idea
Removal of contact and new contact happen in the same instant, forcing adjacency.

In this passage, the author presents a second logical demonstration that the contact points in a moving sphere are adjacent. The argument hinges on the instantaneous nature of contact and its removal. By examining the precise moment of disengagement, we see that a new contact must occur simultaneously, thereby establishing adjacency. This reasoning supports the atomistic view of time composed of discrete instants.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before analyzing.
Notice the footnote marker on 'دفعة' — it may indicate a reference or variant.
2
Understand the instantaneous premise
Recognize that both contact and its removal are said to occur 'instantaneously' (daf'atan). This is a key assumption of the argument.
In kalam, time is composed of indivisible instants.
3
Follow the logical deduction
At the first instant of removal of contact from point 1, contact must occur at point 2. Otherwise there would be a gap.
4
Derive adjacency
Since the two contacts occur in successive instants, the points are adjacent (mutashāfi'a). This supports the idea that the moving object traverses points one by one.
Adjacency here implies no gap between contact points.
5
Reflect on implications
Consider how this argument strengthens the atomistic view of motion and time against the Aristotelian continuous view.
This is part of a larger debate in Islamic philosophy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في تقرير هذا المطلوب : أن نقول : الملاقاة بالنقطة الأولى حصلت دفعة (۱) . وكذلك حصول اللاملاقاة بها ، يحصل دفعة ، ثم يستمر في كل الزمان الذي بعده . ففي أول حصول اللاملاقاة بالنقطة الأولى لا شك أنه حصلت الملاقاة بنقطة ثانية . وحينئذ يلزم تشافع هاتين النقطتين . وهو المطلوب .
The second way of establishing this desired result: We say: Contact at the first point occurred instantaneously (daf'atan). Likewise, the removal of contact from it occurs instantaneously, then it continues in all the time after that. So at the first moment of removal of contact from the first point, there is no doubt that contact has occurred at a second point. And then the adjacency of these two points is necessitated. That is the desired result.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage provides a second, distinct argument to prove that contact points are adjacent (mutashāfi'a). The author considers the instant when the first point loses contact. Since contact is removed instantaneously, at that same instant a second point must make contact, otherwise there would be a gap. Thus the two points are adjacent in time, and since they are distinct points, their spatial positions are also adjacent (given that motion is continuous and time is composed of instants). This forces the conclusion that a line composed of these points exists, supporting atomism.

Key Terms
دفعة (instantaneously)
لاملاقاة (removal of contact)
تشافع (adjacency)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that contact removal and new contact happen at different times.
Correction: The author insists they occur in the same instant.

Checkpoint

A) After a delay.
B) At the same instant that contact is removed from the first point.
C) Only after the sphere stops.
D) It does not occur.

Key Takeaway
The second way shows that at the instant of removal of contact from a point, a new contact must occur simultaneously, forcing the points to be adjacent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This argument proves there is no gap between the removal of one contact and the arrival of another. In your spiritual life, do you perceive gaps where you think Allah's mercy or guidance has left you? How does knowing that His action is continuous—like the adjacency of points—challenge your feeling of being abandoned? Will you trust that at the very instant you feel a loss, He is already providing a new contact?
?
The proof hinges on the instantaneousness of both contact and removal. Are there habits or sins you keep repeating because you think you have time to repent later? If you truly believed that every moment is a new creation—including your intentions—how would that urgency change your decision to turn back to Allah right now, not in the next instant? The Second Proof of the Atom: A Moving Line
The author presents a second, stronger proof for the atom using a moving line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a second, stronger proof for the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) based on the motion of a line over another line, and you will be able to explain why the base line must be composed of points.

Core Idea
A moving point proves that a line is made of indivisible points.

The author now presents a second, more powerful proof for the atom. This proof uses a simple geometric scenario: a perpendicular line sliding along a base line. By carefully analyzing what happens during motion—specifically, the contact between the moving line's endpoint and the base—the author forces us to conclude that the base line must be composed of indivisible points. This argument is more direct than the earlier one and avoids certain objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Pay attention to the logical steps: assumption, motion, contact, point reasoning, conclusion.
The passage is dense but the logic is linear.
2
Visualize the scenario
Imagine a vertical line placed on a horizontal line. The vertical line moves from left to right along the horizontal line. Focus on the endpoint of the vertical line as it travels.
3
Understand the contact argument
The author claims motion without contact is inconceivable. The moving line's endpoint must touch every part of the base line. Since the endpoint is a point, what it touches can only be a point.
4
Draw the conclusion
If the base line is only made of the points contacted by the moving point, then the base line is composed of points. Therefore, it is not infinitely divisible—it is made of atoms.
The author explicitly states this is 'stronger and more complete' than the earlier proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الثاني في إثبات الجوهر الفرد : أن نقول : إذا فرضنا خطاً قائماً على خط ، ثم فرضنا الخط القائم، متحركاً على الخط الآخر ، حتى انتهى من أوله إلى آخره. فهذا الخط المتحرك ، قد ماس بطرفه كلية الخط المتحرك عليه . لأن الحركة على الشيء بدون مماسته غير معقول . وهذا يقتضي أن يقال : إن الخط المتحرك عليه ، إنما تولد من أشياء ، ماسها طرف الخط المتحرك . لكن طرف الخط المتحرك نقطة ، والذي تماسه النقطة : نقطة . فالخط المتحرك عليه ، يجب أن يكون مركباً من النقط . وهو المطلوب . واعلم : أن هذا البرهان أقوى وأكمل من الكلام المتقدم . لان الدليل ،
The second proof of the existence of the atom (al-jawhar al-fard): We say: If we assume a line perpendicular to another line, then we assume the perpendicular line moving on the other line until it goes from its beginning to its end. This moving line has with its endpoint come into contact with the entirety of the line upon which it moves, because motion upon something without contacting it is inconceivable. This necessitates saying that the line upon which it moves is generated only from things that the endpoint of the moving line contacted. But the endpoint of the moving line is a point, and that which the point contacts is a point. Therefore the line upon which it moves must be composed of points. That is the desired result. Know that this proof is stronger and more complete than the preceding discussion, because the proof...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents a new, independent proof for the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The author imagines a line standing perpendicular to a base line. The perpendicular line moves along the base from one end to the other. During this motion, the endpoint of the perpendicular line must contact every part of the base line, as motion without contact is inconceivable. The endpoint is a point, and what it contacts can only be a point (since contact of a point with a divisible object would require division). Therefore the base line is composed entirely of points contacted successively by the moving endpoint. Hence the base line is composed of indivisible points, proving atomism. The author notes that this proof is stronger and more complete than the earlier discussion.

Key Terms
البرهان الثاني (second proof)
الجوهر الفرد (atom)
خط قائم على خط (perpendicular line)
نقطة (point)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the moving endpoint contacts continuous intervals of the base line, not discrete points.
Correction: The author argues that because the endpoint is a point, it can only contact a point at any given moment. Therefore the base line is contacted point by point, not continuous intervals.

Checkpoint

A) It is a point.
B) It is a line.
C) It is divisible.
D) It does not contact the base line.

Key Takeaway
The motion of a line over another line, with contact between points, proves that the base line is composed of indivisible points, establishing the existence of the atom.

?

?

The proof argues that a moving point can only contact another point. In your relationship with Allah, do you treat your deeds as discrete atoms—each one individually created and accounted for—or as an undifferentiated mass? What would change if you truly believed that every single action is a separate 'point' of contact with His creation?
