The Water Example: Matter and Division
Second aspect using sea water to examine matter's behavior upon division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that when a body divides, its matter must either be annihilated or reveal actual infinite parts.

Core Idea
Division of matter either annihilates the original or proves pre-existing infinite parts.

This passage presents a key argument using a sea water example to test what happens to matter when a body divides. It explores two main scenarios: either the matter was one or multiple before division. By examining the logical consequences, it shows that infinite division leads to actual infinite parts, a conclusion crucial for understanding the finite nature of bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument and the key terms like هيولى and قسمة.
The passage is dense; reading twice will help.
2
Identify the two main scenarios
The author presents two possibilities: either the matter of the one water was one, or it was multiple from the start. Notice how each leads to a different outcome.
These are labeled as 'if it was one' and 'if we say... the matters were multiple'.
3
Analyze the first scenario
If matter was one, division either leaves it one or makes it multiple. If one, absurdities arise; if multiple, the original matter is annihilated. Trace the logical steps.
Focus on the impossibility of matter remaining one (east and west water being the same essence).
4
Understand the second scenario and conclusion
If matter was multiple from the start, then parts are actually present before division, so if division could be infinite, infinite parts would actually exist. This is the desired conclusion.
The conclusion that infinite parts would be actual is the key point against infinite divisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني في الجواب : إن ماء البحر، حين كان واحداً . إما أن يقال : إن هيولاه كانت واحدة ، أو ما كانت واحدة . فإن كانت واحدة ، فعند انقسام الجسم. إما أن يقال : بقيت تلك الهيولى واحدة كما كانت ، أو انقسمت وتعددت ومحال أن تبقى واحدة ، وإلا لزم أن يقال : الماء الذي بالمشرق ، والماء الذي بالمغرب : ذات واحدة ، قامت [ به (۱) ] صفتان ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل . ولأنه يلزم اجتماع الأمثال في المحال . لأن الأعداد من الجسمية أمور متماثلة في تمام الماهية .
وأما القسم الثاني . وهو أن يقال : لما صار الماء الواحد ماءين : صارت تلك الهيولى الواحدة أيضاً اثنتين . فنقول : فعلى هذا التقدير . كما أن إيراد التقسيم على الماء الواحد ، يوجب إعدام الماء الأول وحدوث ماءين آخرين ، فكذلك هذا التقسيم ، يوجب إعدام الهيولى الأولى وحدوث فردين آخرين من الهيولي . وحينئذ يكون التقسيم إعداماً للجسم الأول ، بحسب هيولاه وبحسب صورته . فيكون التفريق إعداماً له بالكلية .
هذا إذا قلنا : إن الجسم عندما كان واحداً ، كانت هيولاه واحدة . أما إذا قلنا : إنه عندما كان الجسم واحداً ، كانت الهيوليات متعددة ، بحسب عدد الانقسامات الممكنة فيه. فنقول : فعلى هذا التقدير تكون الجسمية القائمة بكل واحدة من تلك الهيوليات، مغايرة للجسمية القائمة بالهيولى الأخرى ، لامتناع قيام الصفة الواحدة بالمحال الكثيرة . وعلى هذا التقدير فقد كانت الكثرة موجودة بالفعل ، قبل ورود التقسيم . فوجب كون تلك الأجزاء موجودة بالفعل . فثبت : أن الجسم لو كان قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها ، لكانت الأجزاء التي لا نهاية لها ، حاصلة فيه بالفعل . وذلك هو المطلوب
And the second aspect in the answer: Indeed, the water of the sea, when it was one. It is either said: its matter (hayula) was one, or it was not one. If it was one, then at the division of the body. It is either said: that matter remained one as it was, or it divided and multiplied. And it is impossible that it remains one, otherwise it would be necessary to say: the water in the east and the water in the west are one essence, having two attributes, and it is known that that is false. And because it necessitates the gathering of similars in one subject, because the individualities from body-ness are similar in complete essence.
As for the second division, which is: it is said: when the one water became two waters, that one matter also became two. We say: upon this assumption, just as the application of division to the one water necessitates the annihilation of the first water and the occurrence of two other waters, so too this division necessitates the annihilation of the first matter and the occurrence of two other individuals of matter. And then the division is an annihilation of the first body, according to its matter and according to its form. So the separation is an annihilation of it entirely.
This if we say: when the body was one, its matter was one. But if we say: when the body was one, the matters were multiple, according to the number of possible divisions in it. We say: upon this assumption, the body-ness subsisting in each one of those matters is different from the body-ness subsisting in the other matter, due to the impossibility of one attribute subsisting in many subjects. And upon this assumption, multiplicity was actually existent before the occurrence of division. So it is necessary that those parts be actually existent. So it is established: that if the body were receptive to infinite divisions, then the infinite parts would be actually present in it. And that is the required [conclusion].
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is the second aspect of an answer, using an example of sea water to analyze what happens to matter when a body divides. The author sets up two initial possibilities: the matter of the water was one or not one. If it was one, then upon division the matter either remains one or becomes multiple. If it remains one, absurdities arise: water in the east and west would be the same essence with two attributes, and like would be in the same subject—both impossible. If it becomes multiple, then division annihilates the original matter and generates two new ones, so the original body is destroyed entirely. The author then considers another scenario: if the body’s matter was multiple from the start, then multiplicity is actual before division. The conclusion is that if a body could be divided infinitely, it would actually contain infinite parts, which is the required result (likely that bodies have finite indivisible parts).

Key Terms
هيولى
قسمة
إعدام
جسمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Division does not affect the matter itself; matter remains identical throughout.
Correction: The argument shows that if matter remained one, absurdities follow; if it becomes multiple, the original matter is annihilated. Thus matter is not unaffected by division.

Checkpoint

A) It remains the same.
B) It is annihilated and two new matters occur.
C) It multiplies infinitely.
D) It becomes formless.

Key Takeaway
The division of a body cannot leave matter unchanged; it either destroys the original matter or implies actual infinite parts.

Third Proof: Inherent Distinction of Sides
Third proof that side distinction is inherent, not caused by accidents or indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof that the distinction between sides of a body is inherent and not caused by indication or accidents, and why alternative explanations lead to circularity.

Core Idea
Distinction between sides is not caused by pointing or accidents—it must be inherent.

In this proof, the author presents a powerful argument that the distinction between the two sides of a body is not a product of our pointing or of the accidents that reside in it. He sets up two possibilities and shows both lead to circular reasoning, forcing the conclusion that the distinction is preexistent and inherent. This argument supports the existence of actual parts in the body before division.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it, then the English translation. Get a sense of the overall argument.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The author presents a dichotomy: either the distinction between sides arises from our pointing (ishāra) or it is preexistent. Locate these two options in the text.
3
Understand the first circularity argument
The author rejects the first possibility because pointing presupposes a distinction in the thing pointed to, leading to circularity (dawr). Trace this reasoning.
4
Understand the second circularity argument
The author rejects the second possibility by showing that different accidents (a'rād) require prior distinction between sides, again leading to circularity.
5
Grasp the conclusion
With both alternatives refuted, the author concludes that the distinction is preexistent and that parts actually exist in the body before division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إنا لما نظرنا إلى هذا الجسم. فإنا نعلم بالضرورة : أن أحد جانبيه مغاير للجانب الآخر. فإما أن يقال : إن هذه المغايرة إنما حصلت بسبب هاتين الإشارتين ، أو كانت حاصلة قبل هذه الإشارة . والأول باطل . لأن الامتياز في الإشارة ، مشروط بحصول الامتياز في المشار إليه . فلو جعلنا الامتياز في المشار إليه ، معللاً بالامتياز في الإشارة ، وقع الدور . وهو محال
وأيضاً : أجمعنا على أن عند اختلاف الأعراض ، يجب حصول الامتياز . لكن صحة حلول الأعراض المتضادة في الجانبين ، مشروطة بامتياز أحد الجانبين عن الآخر. فلو عللنا ذلك الامتياز بحلول هذين العرضين المختلفين ، لزم الدور . وهو محال . ولما ثبت هذا ، ظهر أن ذلك الامتياز ، كان حاصلا قبل حصول الإشارة ، وقبل حلول الأعراض المختلفة . وذلك يوجب أن الجسم لما كان قابلاً للقسمة ، فقد كانت تلك الأجزاء موجودة فيه بالفعل ، متميزا بعضها عن البعض ، بحسب الخصوصية والتعين . وهو المطلوب
The third proof: Indeed, when we consider this body, we know necessarily that one of its two sides is different from the other side. So it is either said: that this difference occurred only because of these two indications (ishāratayn), or it was existent before this indication. The first is false, because the distinction in the indication is conditioned by the existence of distinction in the indicated. So if we make the distinction in the indicated explained by the distinction in the indication, circularity occurs, which is impossible. Also: we all agree that when accidents (a'rād) differ, distinction must occur. But the validity of the subsistence of contrary accidents in the two sides is conditioned by the distinction of one side from the other. So if we explain that distinction by the subsistence of these two different accidents, circularity occurs, which is impossible. And when this is established, it becomes clear that that distinction was present before the occurrence of the indication and before the subsistence of different accidents. And that necessitates that when the body was receptive to division, those parts were actually existent in it, distinguished from one another by particularity and specification. And that is the required [conclusion].
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof, which argues that the distinction between the two sides of a body is not caused by our act of pointing or by the accidents that reside in the body. The author sets up a dichotomy: the difference either arises from our pointing (ishāra) or is preexistent. The first is rejected because pointing presupposes a distinction in the thing pointed to, leading to circularity. Similarly, if we try to explain the distinction by the presence of different accidents (such as black and white), that also presupposes a prior distinction between the sides for the accidents to reside in, again circular. Therefore, the distinction must be inherent and preexistent, proving that the body actually contains distinct parts before any division, by virtue of particularity and specification.

Key Terms
مغايرة
إشارة
أعراض
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the distinction between sides is caused by our pointing or by the accidents.
Correction: The author shows both lead to circularity: pointing presupposes distinction, and accidents require prior distinction to subsist.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the third proof?
A) The sides of a body are not truly distinct.
B) The distinction of sides is caused by our pointing.
C) The distinction of sides is caused by accidents.
D) The distinction of sides is inherent and preexistent.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between sides of a body is inherent and preexistent, not caused by pointing or accidents, implying actual parts exist before division.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You regularly rely on external markers—your job, your appearance, others' opinions—to define who you are. If your very body's sides are inherently distinct and not defined by accidents, what does that say about your identity being tied to temporary, accidental things? Are you willing to let go of those and ground your worth in what is inherent—your creation by Allah and your soul?
?
The argument destroys circular reasoning. In your prayer, repentance, or striving, do you ever fall into a circle: 'I will change when I feel ready, and I will feel ready when I change'? Where in your life are you trapped in a loop, and will you break it by acting on the truth you know, even without the feeling?
?
The proof concludes that the body contains actual parts before any division. Your limbs and senses are not neutral tools; they have a specific reality given by Allah. How are you using your hands, tongue, and eyes right now? Will you let them be used for what they were actually created for—worship and obedience—or will you pretend they are empty until you decide to act?

Fourth Proof: Unique Ratios of Sections
Fourth proof using a line's sections to show each section has a unique ratio, proving actual distinctness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fourth proof uses the unique receptivity of each possible section of a line to a single ratio to demonstrate that actual distinctions exist within a continuum.

Core Idea
Each section of a line is uniquely tied to one ratio, proving actual distinctness.

In this lesson, we explore the fourth proof presented by the author. It builds on a simple rational insight: if one side has a property the other lacks, then they are actually different. Then it applies this to a line, showing that each possible division point (e.g., half, third) has a unique specific ratio that no other point can have. This demonstrates that these points are predetermined and actually distinct, supporting the existence of actual parts in a body.

The proof begins with a rational intuition: whenever one of the two sides has a characteristic that the other lacks, the difference is actual. This is a key logical foundation.
The author states that the opponents also accept this.
3
Analyze the example of the line
Assume a specific line. Notice that each section (half, third, etc.) is unique and cannot serve as another section. The half-section cannot accept trisection.
This shows that each point is predetermined for a specific ratio.
4
Identify the conclusion
From the fact that each section is uniquely receptive to one ratio, it follows that the sections are actually distinct. This supports the existence of actual parts in a continuum.
The text cuts off but the conclusion is implied.
5
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does this matter? It provides a rational demonstration that potential parts in a body are actually distinct, countering the view that only mind-dependent distinctions exist.

And if it is established that each one of the possible sections is specified (1) by a characteristic

This passage presents the fourth proof, starting with a rational intuition: whenever one side has a property that the other lacks, an actual difference exists. The author then applies this to a line, assuming it is a continuum. On that line, each specific division point (e.g., halfway, one-third) is unique and cannot serve as a different division (e.g., the halfway point cannot also be the one-third point). The Third Proof: Pre-Existing Distinction Requires Actual Parts
The author presents the third proof for actual parts from necessary distinction of sides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof for the existence of actual parts in a body by showing that the distinction between sides must be prior to mental indication and accidents, leading to the conclusion that parts actually exist.

Core Idea
Distinction between sides cannot depend on our pointing or on accidents – it must be pre-existing.

This passage presents a powerful argument from the necessary distinction of the sides of a body. The author demonstrates that this distinction cannot be caused by our mental acts of pointing, nor by the different accidents that may occupy those sides. Instead, it must be inherent and pre-existing, which implies that the body actually contains distinct parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author’s own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the dichotomous structure: 'either…or'.
2
Identify the two rejected options
The author considers two possible causes for the distinction between sides: mental indication and different accidents. Find where each is introduced and how they are refuted using circularity.
Circularity (دور) is the key logical flaw.
3
Understand the conclusion
After rejecting both options, the author concludes that distinction exists prior to both, implying actual parts. Ask yourself why this conclusion follows.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إنا لما نظرنا إلى هذا الجسم. فإنا نعلم بالضرورة : أن أحد جانبيه مغاير للجانب الآخر. فإما أن يقال : إن هذه المغايرة إنما حصلت بسبب هاتين الإشارتين ، أو كانت حاصلة قبل هذه الإشارة . والأول باطل . لأن الامتياز في الإشارة ، مشروط بحصول الامتياز في المشار إليه . فلو جعلنا الامتياز في المشار إليه ، معللاً بالامتياز في الإشارة ، وقع الدور . وهو محال وأيضاً : أجمعنا على أن عند اختلاف الأعراض ، يجب حصول الامتياز . لكن صحة حلول الأعراض المتضادة في الجانبين ، مشروطة بامتياز أحد الجانبين عن الآخر. فلو عللنا ذلك الامتياز بحلول هذين العرضين المختلفين ، لزم الدور . وهو محال . ولما ثبت هذا ، ظهر أن ذلك الامتياز ، كان حاصلا قبل حصول الإشارة ، وقبل حلول الأعراض المختلفة . وذلك يوجب أن الجسم لما كان قابلاً للقسمة ، فقد كانت تلك الأجزاء موجودة فيه بالفعل ، متميزا بعضها عن البعض ، بحسب الخصوصية والتعين . وهو المطلوب
The third proof: When we consider this body, we necessarily know that one side is different from the other. Then it must be said: either this difference occurred due to these two indications, or it existed before this indication. The first is invalid because distinction in the indication is conditioned upon the occurrence of distinction in the indicated. If we make the distinction in the indicated caused by the distinction in the indication, circularity occurs, and it is impossible. Also: we all agree that when accidents differ, distinction must occur. But the validity of contradictory accidents subsisting in the two sides is conditioned upon the distinction of one side from the other. If we attributed that distinction to the subsistence of these two different accidents, circularity would follow, and it is impossible. And when this is established, it becomes clear that that distinction existed before the occurrence of the indication and before the subsistence of the different accidents. That necessitates that since the body was divisible, those parts existed in it actually, distinguished from each other by particularity and determination. And that is what was desired.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of actual parts in a body. The author begins by stating a necessary observation: when we look at a body, we find that one side is different from the other. He then presents a dichotomy: either this difference arises from the two mental indications (اشارتين) we make, or it was present before those indications. The first option is rejected because distinction in the indication depends on prior distinction in the indicated thing; otherwise circularity occurs. Next, he adds a second argument: it is agreed that when different accidents occur, distinction must take place. But for contradictory accidents to subsist in two sides, those sides must already be distinct. If we try to explain the distinction of the sides by the accidents subsisting in them, circularity again follows. Thus, the distinction must have existed before both the mental indication and the accidents. This proves that since the body is divisible, its parts exist in actuality, distinguished by their particularity and determination. That is the desired conclusion.

امتياز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the difference between two sides of a body is merely a result of our mental pointing or of the accidents that inhabit those sides.
Correction: The argument shows that both explanations lead to circularity: distinction in pointing presupposes prior distinction, and contradictory accidents require already distinct sides. Hence the distinction must be inherent and pre-existing.

Checkpoint

A) Because the indication requires pre-existing distinction in the indicated.
B) Because the indications are not real.
C) Because the sides are identical.
D) Because the indication causes the distinction.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between the sides of a body must be intrinsic and prior to any external factors, proving that parts exist actually.

?
This proof exposes the fallacy of circular reasoning. In your own beliefs, where might you be guilty of assuming what you want to prove? How can you root your faith in authentic evidence rather than convenient assumptions?

The Fourth Proof: Infinite Divisibility Implies Actual Infinite Parts
The author presents the fourth proof for atomism using specificity of division points.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that infinite divisibility of a line would necessitate actual infinite parts, thus proving the existence of indivisible atoms.

Core Idea
Infinite divisibility leads to an actual infinite, which is impossible.

In this lesson, we examine the fourth proof for atomism, which uses the specificity of division points to show that a line cannot be infinitely divisible. The argument proceeds by assuming a line, identifying its unique division points for different ratios, and then deducing that if there were infinitely many such points, they would have to exist actually. Since an actual infinite is impossible, the line must be composed of a finite number of indivisible parts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundational premise
The proof begins with a premise accepted by all sides: if one side has a property lacking in the other, actual distinction exists. This sets the stage for the argument.
This premise is crucial for the later inference.
2
Follow the thought experiment of a line
Imagine a specific line. It has definite half-point, third-point, quarter-point, etc. Each point is uniquely suited to accept a specific ratio (e.g., half) and cannot accept others.
The uniqueness of each division point is key.
3
Identify the consequence of infinite possible points
If there were infinitely many possible division points (since division can go on indefinitely), then each point would have a unique property. Therefore, these points would have to exist actually, leading to an actual infinite number of parts.
This step directly leads to the conclusion.
4
Consider the objection and response
An objector says that ratios like half only exist after actual parts exist. The author replies that we do not need to prove existence of parts; rather, the capabilities for ratios are real distinct states. Each point has a unique capability, and these capabilities are actual.
The response strengthens the argument by focusing on capabilities.
5
Conclude the proof
Since an actual infinite is impossible, the line cannot have infinitely many division points. Thus, the line is composed of a finite number of indivisible parts (atoms).
This conclusion supports the doctrine of atomism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : صريح العقل مساعد على أنه مهما اختص أحد الجانبين ، بخاصية مفقودة في الجانب الآخر. فإن المغايرة حاصلة بالفعل . والقوم أيضاً ساعدوا عليه . إذا ثبت هذا ، فلنفرض خطاً معيناً ، فنقول : لا شك أن مقطع النصف فيه معين ، ومقطع الثلث فيه معين، وكذا مقطع الربع والخمس ، وسائر المقاطع التي لا نهاية لها . والمقطع الذي يقبل التنصيف يستحيل أن يقبل سائر الأقسام . أعني : التثليث والتربيع . فإن كل مقطع فرض قابلاً لنسبة معينة . فإن زيد على ذلك المقطع : القليل أو الكثير . فإنه لا يبقى البتة قابلاً لتلك النسبة . فثبت : أن كل واحد من المقاطع الممكنة ، فإنه مخصوص بقبول نسبة معينة ، بمعنى أنه يجب كونها قابلاً لتلك النسبية . ويمتنع كونه قابلاً لنسبة أخرى . وإذا ثبت أن كل واحد من المقاطع الممكنة مخصوص بخاصية توجب قبول نسبة معينة . فلو كانت المقاطع الممكنة غير متناهية ، لزم كونها حاصلة بالفعل . فإن قالوا : هذه الأوصاف . أعني : كونه نصفاً وثلثاً وربعاً ، لا تحصل إلا بعد حصول الأجزاء بالفعل ، ونحن لا نساعد على حصول تلك الأجزاء فيها بالفعل . فنقول في الجواب : لا حاجة بنا إلى إثبات ما ذكرتم . بل نقول قبول نسبة النصف بعينها مخصوص بمقطع معين ، ويستحيل حصول تلك النسبة في مقطع غيره . وكذا القول في الثلث والربع . فإن كل واحد من تلك المقاطع مخصوصاً بقبول نسبة معينة ، وكان قبول تلك النسبة ممتنع الثبوت لعينه ولذاته في سائر المقاطع . فثبت : أن كل واحد منها مختص بقابلية نسبة بعينها ، وهذه القابليات أحوال حاصلة في نفس الأمر . فيلزم : أن الخط المعين ، لو كان قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها ، لكان مركباً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل . ومعلوم : أن هذا محال . والله أعلم
The fourth proof: Clear reason supports that whenever one side is distinguished by a property lacking in the other, then actual difference exists. And the opponents also agreed upon it. If this is established, then let us assume a specific line, and we say: No doubt that its half-point is specific, its third-point is specific, and similarly the quarter-point and fifth-point, and the rest of the points without end. And the point that accepts halving cannot possibly accept the other divisions, namely tritave and quartering. For every point assumed is capable of a specific ratio. If that point is increased by a little or a lot, it absolutely does not remain capable of that ratio. So it is established that every one of the possible points is specified by acceptance of a specific ratio, meaning that it must be capable of that ratio and cannot be capable of another ratio. And if it is established that every possible point is specified by a property necessitating acceptance of a specific ratio, then if the possible points were infinite, they would necessarily be actual. If they say: These descriptions, namely its being half, third, and quarter, do not occur except after the actual existence of parts, and we do not concede the actual existence of those parts in it. We say in response: We have no need to prove what you mentioned. Rather we say: The acceptance of the specific half-ratio is particular to a specific point, and it is impossible for that ratio to occur in another point. And likewise for the third and quarter. For each one of those points is particularized to accept a specific ratio, and the acceptance of that ratio is impossible in its essence and self in all other points. So it is established that each one of them is specific to a capability for a specific ratio, and these capabilities are states existing in reality. Consequently, the specific line, if it were capable of infinite divisions, would be composed of infinite actual parts. And it is known that this is impossible. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the actual existence of indivisible parts (atoms) in a body. The author begins with a premise accepted by all: when one side has a property lacking in the other, actual distinction exists. Then he sets up a thought experiment: take a specific line. It has a definite half-point, third-point, quarter-point, etc. The point that allows bisection cannot allow trisection or quartering. Each point is uniquely suited to a specific ratio. If you add or subtract anything from that point, it no longer accepts that ratio. Thus each possible point has a specific property that determines which ratio it can accept. If these possible points were infinite in number, they would have to exist actually (since each is determinate). An objector says: these ratios (half, third, etc.) only exist after actual parts exist; we do not concede that those parts actually exist. The author responds: we do not need to prove that. Instead, we argue that the acceptance of the half-ratio is specific to a certain point, and it is impossible for that ratio to occur in any other point. Each point has a unique capability for a specific ratio. These capabilities are real states. Therefore, if a line were capable of infinite divisions, it would have to contain an infinite number of actual parts. But that is impossible (because infinite actual magnitude is impossible). Hence the line must be composed of a finite number of actual parts.

Key Terms
مقطع
نسبة
قبول
قابلية
انقسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite divisibility does not imply actual infinite parts because division points are only potential.
Correction: The proof shows that each possible division point has a unique, determinate property (capability for a specific ratio). If there were infinitely many such points, these properties would be actual distinctions, leading to an actual infinite. Hence the line cannot be infinitely divisible.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the fourth proof?
A) A line cannot be divided.
B) A line is composed of a finite number of actual parts.
C) A line has no parts.
D) Division points are infinite.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof demonstrates that a line must be composed of a finite number of indivisible parts because infinite divisibility would entail actual infinite parts, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that every point on a line is uniquely determined by Allah to accept only one specific ratio. Reflect: In your own life, every moment and every action is also uniquely determined by Him. Are you living with the awareness that each decision you make is a unique point in your life that cannot be repeated? How does this change your sense of responsibility for each moment?
?
If infinite actual parts are impossible in the physical world, then your life has a finite number of moments. Do you act as if you have infinite time, procrastinating on obligations? What will you do today to make better use of your finite time?
?
The opponents argued that the ratios only exist after actual division. But the author insisted that the capabilities are real even before. Think of your own good deeds: does their reward depend only on the outcome, or is the intention (capability) itself actual and recorded by Allah? How does this motivate you to purify your intentions right now, even before you act?

The Fifth Proof: Unity is the Essence Itself
Author presents the fifth proof that unity is the essence itself, using a reductio ad infinitum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that unity is identical to the individual essence and why it cannot be a separate attribute.

Core Idea
Unity is not an extra tag—it is the thing itself.

We now examine the fifth proof, which tackles a subtle but critical point: is 'oneness' something added to an essence, or is it simply the essence itself? The author uses a logical argument to show that if unity were an addition, infinite regress would result. This conclusion has profound implications for understanding change and annihilation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the argument is incomplete here; it continues on the next page.
2
Identify the conditional argument
The author starts with a hypothesis: 'if unity were an added attribute...' Follow the logical steps from that hypothesis to the impossibility.
3
Understand the infinite regress problem
Why would distinguishing unities by another unity lead to infinite regress? Grasp this key point.
Infinite regress is considered impossible in classical kalam.
4
Apply the conclusion to a body becoming two
The author applies the result to the case of a body changing from one to two. Consider what this implies about essence and annihilation.
The full conclusion is not in this window.

الحجة الخامسة : إن وحدة الشيء ، عبارة عن ذاته المتعينة المتشخصة لأن الوحدة لو كانت صفة زائدة على تلك الذات المتعينة ، لكانت الوحدات متساوية في ماهية كونها وحدة فيكون امتياز كل واحد من أجزاء هذه الماهية عن الآخر ، بوحدة أخرى. ولزم التسلسل . وهو محال . فثبت : أن وحدة كل شيء، عبارة عن ذاته المتعينة المتشخصة . وإذا ثبت هذا ، لزم أن يقال : إن زوال تلك الوحدة يقتضي فناء تلك الذات المتعينة . إذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : لو كان الجسم واحداً في نفسه ، فإذا صار : اثنين ، وجب الحكم بأن تلك الذات التي كانت موجودة قد عدمت وفنيت وحدثت ذاتان متفاوتان متغايرتان للذات الأولى . ولما كان ذلك
The fifth proof: The unity of a thing is its particular and individual essence. Because if unity were an added attribute to that particular essence, then unities would be equal in the quiddity of being unity, and the distinction of each part of this quiddity from another would be by another unity, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. So it is established that the unity of each thing is its particular and individual essence. And when this is established, it must be said that the removal of that unity necessitates the annihilation of that particular essence. When this is established, we say: If a body were one in itself, then when it becomes two, it must be judged that that essence which existed has ceased and perished, and two distinct essences, different from the first essence, have come into being. And when that is so...
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a proof that unity is not an attribute added to the essence but is the essence itself. The author argues: if unity were a superadded attribute, then all unities would share the same quiddity of being unity. To distinguish one unity from another, there would need to be another unity, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible. Therefore, unity must be the particular individual essence itself. Consequently, if unity is lost, the essence itself is annihilated. Applying this to a body: if a body that is one becomes two, the original essence must have perished and two new essences come into existence. The argument is incomplete in this window; it continues on the next page.

Misconception: Unity is an additional attribute that can be separated from the essence.
Correction: The argument shows that if unity were an addition, infinite regress would result; therefore unity must be identical to the essence itself.

Checkpoint

A) Unity is an attribute added to the essence.
B) Unity is identical to the individual essence.
C) Unity is separate from the essence.
D) Unity is not real.

Key Takeaway
Unity is not a separate attribute; it is the individual essence itself, so losing unity means the essence ceases to exist.

?
The author says removal of unity entails annihilation. If you were to lose your sense of purpose (your ‘unity’ of intention), would your current self cease to exist? What new self would emerge—and are you prepared to face that?

Response to Philosophers: Proving the Indivisible Atom
This passage discusses the theological implication of the proofs and refutes the philosophers' objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mutakallimūn defend atomism by refuting infinite parts and respond to the philosophers' objection that bodies are not composed of parts at all.

Core Idea
Refuting infinite divisibility does not automatically prove atomism—philosophers deny composition entirely.

This passage presents the conclusion that mutakallimūn draw from the previous proofs: since bodies cannot have infinite parts, they must have finite parts—the indivisible atom. However, philosophers object that disproving infinite parts does not prove finite composition because they believe bodies are single continuous substances. The author then shows how the proofs are still effective in refuting the philosophers' position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mutakallimūn's conclusion
Notice that they equate disproving infinite parts with proving atomism: since bodies cannot have infinite parts, they must be composed of finite parts (the indivisible atom).
2
Grasp the philosophers' objection
Philosophers argue that the conclusion does not follow because they reject composition altogether—bodies are simple, continuous wholes, so disproving infinite parts is irrelevant.
This is a fundamental disagreement about the nature of bodies.
3
See the author's counter-response
The author argues that the proofs actually show that bodies cannot be receptive to infinite divisions, which directly contradicts the philosophers' view that bodies are infinitely divisible. Thus the proofs are useful.
The key is that the philosophers believe in potential infinite divisibility, which the proofs refute.
4
Reflect on the dialectic
Appreciate that the debate is not just about atoms but about whether bodies are composite or simple. Each side uses different starting assumptions.
This passage shows how theological arguments must address opposing metaphysical frameworks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن المتكلمين كانوا يقولون : لما بطل هذا المذهب ، فقد ثبت القول بالجوهر الفرد . وأما الفلاسفة : فقد استبعدوا هذا الكلام ، وحكموا على صاحبه بالجهل ، وقلة الفهم . وقالوا : إنه لا يلزم من إبطال تركب الجسم من أجزاء لا نهاية لها ، كونه مركباً من أجزاء متناهية. بل الحق : أن الجسم في نفسه شيء واحد ، ليس مركباً البتة من الأجزاء . وحينئذ لا يبقى في ذكر هذه الدلائل منفعة في إبطال قولنا ومذهبنا . واعلم : أنا بينا بالوجوه القاطعة اليقينية : أن الجسم لو كان قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها ، لوجب كونه مركباً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها . فإذا ذكرنا هذه الدلائل في بيان أنه يمتنع كون الجسم مؤلفاً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل . فحينئذ يلزم فساد المقدم ، وهو كونه قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها . وعلى هذا الطريق فإن هذه الدلائل ينتفع بها في إبطال قول الفلاسفة . والله أعلم
And know that the mutakallimūn used to say: Since this doctrine has been invalidated, the statement of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) is established. As for the philosophers (al-falāsifa), they found this speech far-fetched, and judged its author as ignorant and lacking understanding. They said: It does not follow from the invalidation of the composition of the body from infinite parts that it is composed of finite parts. Rather, the truth is that the body in itself is a single thing, not composed at all of parts. In that case, there remains no benefit in mentioning these proofs to invalidate our statement and doctrine. And know: We have demonstrated by certain and definitive proofs that if the body were receptive to infinite divisions, then it would necessarily be composed of infinite parts. So when we mention these proofs in explaining that it is impossible for the body to be composed of actually infinite parts, then the invalidity of the premise follows, which is its being receptive to infinite divisions. And in this way, these proofs are useful in refuting the statement of the philosophers. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a theological and philosophical commentary on the preceding proofs. The mutakallimūn (theologians) conclude that since bodies cannot have infinite parts, they must be composed of finite parts, which is the doctrine of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The philosophers (falāsifa) object that disproving infinite parts does not prove finite parts, because they hold that bodies are not composed of parts at all—they are a single continuous substance. Thus, they argue the proofs are irrelevant. The author responds by asserting that the proofs demonstrate the impossibility of a body being receptive to infinite divisions. Since that premise (being receptive to infinite divisions) is false, the proofs do refute the philosophers' claim that bodies are infinitely divisible. Therefore, the proofs are useful in defending the mutakallimūn's position. The author ends with 'Allah knows best'.

فلاسفة
جوهر فرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Disproving infinite parts automatically proves atomism without considering alternative views.
Correction: The philosophers deny that bodies are composed of parts at all, so disproving infinite parts does not automatically establish atomism unless one also refutes the continuous substance view.

Checkpoint

C) Because they believe in atoms

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimūn's proofs against infinite parts are used to support atomism, but they require an additional argument against the philosophers' alternative view that bodies are continuous wholes.

If the philosophers were correct that the body is a simple unity, then the mutakallimūn's entire project of proving atoms would be a waste. Defending Atomism: Response to Ibn Sina's Objection
Proof for atom, Ibn Sina's objection, and the author's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends the proof for the indivisible atom against Ibn Sina's objection by showing that the absurd consequence only follows from infinite divisibility, not from atomism.

Core Idea
The absurdity of infinite sheets from a mustard seed only proves infinite divisibility false, not atomism.

The author has just presented a proof for the indivisible atom based on an absurd consequence of infinite divisibility. Now he must defend it against a powerful objection from Ibn Sina, who argues that the same absurdity follows from atomism. In this passage, we see a careful logical response: the author distinguishes between what is known to be impossible by necessity and what is merely unknown, showing that the objection fails and the original proof stands.

Guided Path
1
Read the entire passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full argument. Notice the flow: proof, objection, answer.
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'لوجاز', 'قال', 'والجواب'.
2
Analyze the proof and objection
Identify the structure of the author's proof and how Ibn Sina tries to reverse it. Ask yourself: Why does Ibn Sina think his objection refutes the proof?
Ibn Sina claims the same absurd consequence follows from atomism, so the proof is not decisive.
3
Examine the answer
The author gives two points: (1) With atomism we know by necessity the consequence is impossible, (2) Even if we don't, it's only a possibility, unlike infinite divisibility where it's certain. Understand why this defeats Ibn Sina's objection.
The key difference is certainty vs. mere possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثامن في ذكر بقية الدلائل الحالة في الثبات الجوهر الفرد. الحجة الأولى : إن الجسم لو كان قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها ، لجاز أن ينفصل من الخردلة الواحدة ، صفائح يغشى بها أطباق العرش والكرم والسموات والأرضين ، لا مرة واحدة ، بل ألف مرة . ومعلوم أن ذلك في غاية البعد. قال الشيخ الرئيس : ( هذا أيضاً لازم على القائلين بإثبات الجوهر الفرد . لأن مع القول بكون الجسم مركباً من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ، لا يبعد أن يحصل في الخردلة صفائح يغشى بها وجه السموات والأرضين . وإذا كان هذا المحذور لازماً على الكل ، فقد زال الاستبعاد » . والجواب عنه : إن مع القول بإثبات الجوهر الفرد ، نعلم بالضرورة : أن ذلك محال . سلمنا : أنه يبقى احتماله ، إلا أنه احتمال ، لا يعرف ، أنه هل هو ممكن ، أو ممتنع في نفسه ؟ وإن كنا لا نعرف امتناعه - أما على القول بنفي الجوهر الفرد ، فإنا نقطع بأن هذا الذي ألزمناه ، يكون ممكن الوقوع لا مرة واحدة ، بل مراراً لا نهاية لها لأنه لا صفحة توجد من تلك الخردلة ، إلا وهي قابلة لانقسامات غير متناهية . وكل واحد منها ، فإنه يقبل الانقسامات التي لا نهاية لها مرة واحدة فثبت : أن هذا المحال ، إنما يلزم على قول من يقول : إن الجسم يقبل انقسامات لا نهاية لها .
The eighth chapter on mentioning the remaining proofs concerning the establishment of the indivisible atom. The first proof: If the body were divisible into infinite divisions, then it would be possible that from a single mustard seed there separate sheets that cover the layers of the Throne, the Footstool, the heavens, and the earths, not once but a thousand times. And it is known that this is extremely far-fetched. The Chief Master (Ibn Sina) said: 'This is also necessary upon those who affirm the indivisible atom. Because with the statement that the body is composed of parts that do not divide, it is not far that in a mustard seed there occur sheets covering the face of the heavens and the earths. And if this objection is necessary upon all, then the improbability is removed.' The answer to it: With the affirmation of the indivisible atom, we know by necessity that that is impossible. We grant that its possibility remains, but it is a possibility that is not known whether it is possible or impossible in itself. And even if we do not know its impossibility, upon the negation of the indivisible atom, we are certain that what we have required is possible of occurrence, not once but infinite times, because there is no sheet from that mustard seed except that it is divisible into infinite divisions. And each one of them accepts infinite divisions once. So it is established that this impossibility only follows the statement of one who says that the body accepts infinite divisions.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair within a broader discussion of proofs for the indivisible atom (جوهر فرد). The author first presents a proof by absurdity: if a body were infinitely divisible, then from a single mustard seed one could extract sheets covering the entire cosmos—a manifest absurdity. Ibn Sina (الشيخ الرئيس) objects that the same absurdity applies to the atomist position, since a mustard seed composed of atoms could also be arranged into vast sheets, so the absurdity is common and thus not a valid argument. The author's answer carefully refutes this. First, with atomism we know by necessity that such a thing is impossible, because atoms are indivisible fixed units. Even if one grants a mere possibility, it is unknown whether that possibility is actually possible or impossible—it remains a bare unknown. In contrast, under the denial of atoms (i.e., infinite divisibility), we are certain that the required outcome is possible, indeed possible an infinite number of times, because every resulting sheet is itself infinitely divisible. Therefore, the original absurdity necessarily follows only from the premise of infinite divisibility, not from atomism. Thus the objection fails, and the proof remains valid against the opponents of atomism.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد
انقسامات لا نهاية لها
خردلة
الشيخ الرئيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the author is trying to prove atomism outright, without defense.
Correction: The author is defending the proof against a specific objection; he shows the alternative (infinite divisibility) leads to a certain absurdity, while atomism does not.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does Ibn Sina's objection not refute the proof for the indivisible atom?
A) Because with atomism, the claimed absurdity is known to be impossible by necessity.
B) Because the proof is based on divine revelation, not reason.
C) Because Ibn Sina misunderstood the logical structure of the proof.
D) Because the absurdity applies equally to both views, so it is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The proof for the indivisible atom remains valid because the absurd consequence only follows from infinite divisibility, not from atomism.

The author states that under atomism we know by necessity that the imagined consequence is impossible. First Argument: Acute Angles and Infinite Divisibility
Presents a geometrical absurdity to refute infinite divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a geometrical example from kalam refutes the concept of infinite divisibility by showing it leads to an absurd conclusion.

Core Idea
Infinite divisibility leads to a contradiction between growth and shrinkage.

Kalam theologians often used geometrical arguments to challenge philosophical concepts. Here, the author presents a thought experiment involving two types of acute angles to expose the absurdity of infinite divisibility. This argument is not about geometry per se but about the logical consequences of assuming matter can be divided endlessly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Pay attention to the description of the two angles.
2
Identify the two angles
The first angle is formed by two straight lines and decreases infinitely. The second is formed by a perpendicular and a circular arc and increases infinitely.
Notice the terms 'زاوية حادة مستقيمة الخطين' and 'زاوية حادة حادثة من العمود ومن حدبة الدائرة'.
3
Understand the infinite operations
The first angle can be reduced without end, the second can be enlarged without end. Both operations are infinite.
4
Grasp the absurd conclusion
Despite the second angle increasing infinitely, it never surpasses the first angle at any stage of its decrease. This is logically contradictory.
The author calls this 'ba'īd' (far-fetched) and rejected by reason.
5
Connect to infinite divisibility
If magnitudes were infinitely divisible, such absurd geometrical situations would arise. Therefore, infinite divisibility is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير النهاية. فهذه الحادة المستقيمة الخطين تقبل التناقص إلى غير النهاية . وتلك الزاوية الحادة الحادثة من العمود ، ومن حدبة الدائرة ، تتزايد إلى غير النهاية . مع أنها مع جميع مراتب الزيادة، تكون أقل من الزاوية الحادة المستقيمة الخطين ، من جميع مراتب التناقص . وذلك بعيد ، لا يقبله العقل .
To infinity. So this acute angle with two straight lines accepts decrease to infinity. And that acute angle produced from the perpendicular and the arc of the circle increases to infinity. While it, with all degrees of increase, is less than the acute angle with two straight lines, in all degrees of decrease. And that is far-fetched, not accepted by the intellect.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents a geometrical proof against infinite divisibility of magnitudes. The author describes two types of acute angles: one formed by two straight lines that can decrease infinitely, and another formed by a perpendicular and a circular arc that can increase infinitely. Despite the second angle increasing without bound, it always remains smaller than the first angle at any degree of its decrease. This result is considered absurd ('ba'īd') and is rejected by reason ('lā yaqbaluhu al-'aql'). The argument uses the incompatibility of infinite increase and infinite decrease to show that the assumption of infinite divisibility leads to contradiction.

Key Terms
زاوية حادة
غير النهاية
التناقص
التزايد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is a mathematical proof within Euclidean geometry.
Correction: It is a dialectical argument from kalam, using a thought experiment to show the absurdity of infinite divisibility, not a formal geometric proof.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the argument about the two acute angles?
A) To prove that angles can be infinitely divided.
B) To show that infinite divisibility leads to an absurdity.
C) To demonstrate the superiority of Euclidean geometry.
D) To define acute angles precisely.

Key Takeaway
The infinite increase of one acute angle never surpassing the infinite decrease of another is an absurdity that refutes the notion of infinite divisibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the absurdity described—that something infinitely increasing can never surpass something infinitely decreasing—how does this challenge your own assumptions about the physical world around you? Are there beliefs you hold that, upon closer examination, lead to similar contradictions? What might that reveal about the need for a Creator who set limits?
?
This argument uses geometry to make a point about metaphysics. In your own life, are there areas where you rely on mental models or assumptions that, if pushed to their logical end, lead to absurdity? How willing are you to abandon comfortable assumptions for the sake of truth?
?
The author says the conclusion is 'not accepted by the intellect.' Think of a time when your intellect rejected something that seemed obvious or comfortable. Did you follow your intellect or your desires? How does this lesson call you to submit your reason to the truth, even when it is uncomfortable?
